

UPDATE 3-Apple, Tesla ask California to change proposed self-driving car test policy - 路透新闻

{{20170429T001514.671+0000}}UPDATE 3-Apple, Tesla ask California to change proposed self-driving car test policy(Recasts to reflect Apple's stance; adds company quote, details about requests)

By David Shepardson

April 28 (Reuters) - Apple Inc urged California to toughen up its proposed policy on testing self-driving cars, a move that would result in more public data that could help Apple catch up to rivals in the self-driving space by giving it a better window into their strengths and weaknesses.

In a letter made public on Friday, Apple suggested a series of changes to the draft policy that is under development and said it looks forward to working with California and others "so that rapid technology development may be realized while ensuring the safety of the traveling public."

Waymo, the self-driving car unit of Google parent company Alphabet Inc , Ford Motor Co , Uber Technologies Inc [UBER.UL], Toyota Motor Corp <7203.T>, Tesla Motors Inc and others also filed comments suggesting changes.

California said on Tuesday it would review comments before deciding whether to make changes to the policy that aims to allow companies to test vehicles without traditional steering wheels and controls or human back-up drivers. [nL1N1HY1XM]

The state is at the forefront of a crowded race to develop self-driving vehicles and the proposed changes from automakers and technology companies help provide insight into current efforts.

In its letter, Apple said California should revise how companies report self-driving system "disengagements." California currently requires companies to report how many times the self-driving system was deactivated and control handed back to humans because of a system failure or a situation tied to traffic, weather or road conditions that required human intervention for safety reasons.

But Apple wants those rules to extend to humans stepping in to prevent even minor traffic violations. Apple contends the reporting rules as written leave too much wiggle room for car makers and "caused public confusion and misunderstanding," wrote Steve Kenner, Apple's director of product integrity.

Apple also asked regulators to revisit language around the definition of an autonomous vehicle to clarify that permits are required in advanced systems even when a safety driver is present.

The exact wording around when permits are needed became a sticking point between Uber and state officials last year when the California Department of Motor Vehicles ordered Uber to cease its self-driving tests in San Francisco.

Apple also said the state's rules for development vehicles used only in testing could "restrict both the design and equipment that can be used in test vehicles."

A late entrant to the self-driving race, Apple secured a permit earlier this month to test autonomous vehicles in California. Although it has never openly acknowledged it is looking into building a car, Apple has recruited dozens of auto experts. The company declined to comment on Friday.

'STIFLE INNOVATION'

Tesla said California should not bar testing of autonomous vehicles that are 10,000 pounds (4,535 kg) or more, a move that Apple also joined. Tesla said such a move could "stifle innovation," and bar a company from testing a heavy autonomous vehicle that might be used to haul parts on private property rather than on public roads, pushing developers in this sector out of the state.

Elon Musk, chief executive of Tesla, in 2016 announced plans for new electric vehicles, including a commercial truck called the Tesla Semi and a public transport bus. The electric vehicle pioneer said earlier this month it plans to unveil a commercial truck in September.

Tesla also said California should not prohibit the sale of non-self-driving vehicles previously used for autonomous vehicle testing. Tesla said that under the proposal, if it loads a vehicle with autonomous testing software and then replaces it with conventional production software it could be barred from selling the vehicle.

Uber said California should allow paying members of the public to ride in autonomous vehicles with drivers, saying: "There is no reason to deny those riders an opportunity to travel in an autonomous test vehicle and provide honest feedback."

Lyft Inc, a ride-hailing service rival of Uber, asked the state to remove a requirement that it notify local authorities of autonomous vehicle testing.

Waymo asked California to remove its liability proposal. On Tuesday, General Motors Co had said the state's proposed liability rules could make automakers liable regardless of fault for any crash. GM also said that automakers should be allowed to reuse autonomous vehicles and parts after testing or if the vehicle is scrapped.

Volkswagen AG and Daimler AG submitted joint comments seeking changes to the extent of data required to be retained in crashes involving self-driving cars.

A number of automakers have said they plan to begin deploying self-driving vehicles, some in commercial fleets, by 2020-21.

(Reporting by David Shepardson, additional reporting by Alexandria Sage and Stephen Nellis in San Francisco; editing by Frances Kerry and G Crosse) ((David.Shepardson@thomsonreuters.com; +1-202-898-8324))

Tesla must complete brake fix to regain top safety rating -Consumer Reports - 路透新闻

{{20170428T232117.322+0000}}Tesla must complete brake fix to regain top safety rating -Consumer ReportsBy Nick Carey

DETROIT, April 28 (Reuters) - Tesla Inc needs to complete fixing its Model S sedan emergency braking system to regain Consumer Reports' top safety rating, the magazine said on Friday, noting that a recent update by the luxury electric car maker was not enough.

The magazine, which provides an annual rating of vehicles sold in the United States, said on Wednesday the sedan had lost its top ranking in the ultra-luxury car category for failing to install the feature that it had promised to owners as standard equipment. [nL1N1HY0B2]

The Model S fell to third place in Consumer Reports' ratings behind the Lexus LS made by Toyota Motor Corp <7203.T> and the BMW 7 Series .

Consumer Reports said both Tesla models previously came with standard automatic emergency braking (AEB), a feature that helps reduce accidents. The software issue affects more recent vehicles built since late October 2016.

The magazine said Friday that the Model S sedan it owns had received an automatic emergency braking software update Thursday, but the new version only operates up to 28 miles per hour (45 km).

That is far less than the current 90 mile per hour limit for the prior Tesla AEB system included on vehicles built before late October.

The magazine cited a statement from Tesla that "over the next several weeks" the car maker would increase the speed limit "until it is the most capable of any vehicle in the world."

The California automaker last week recalled 53,000 Model S and Model X vehicles to fix an unrelated parking brake issue. [nL3N1HS58J]

Earlier this month, Tesla briefly edged out General Motors Co to become the most valuable U.S. car maker. [nL1N1HI1EI]

(Reporting by Nick Carey; Editing by Richard Chang) ((nick.carey@thomsonreuters.com; +1-312-636-8837))

Tesla says it will stop selling solar door-to-door - 路透新闻

{{20170428T215612.438+0000}}Tesla says it will stop selling solar door-to-doorBy Nichola Groom

April 28 (Reuters) - Tesla Inc on Friday said that its subsidiary SolarCity will curtail door-to-door sales of rooftop solar installations over the next month as Tesla seeks to absorb the company into its high-end brand.

The move comes at a time when growth in sales of residential solar systems has slowed in key states, including California, where Tesla is based. Industry watchers say consumers in more mature solar markets have tired of the industry's aggressive sales tactics.

"We believe this decision reflects what most of our prospective customers prefer, and will result in a better experience for them," a Tesla spokesperson said in an emailed statement.

Tesla has built its luxury electric car brand on exclusivity, whereas SolarCity marketed its systems to a wide range of consumers mainly by promising cost savings.

As a result, the move marks a major shift for SolarCity, which before its acquisition by Tesla had become the nation's top solar installer by amassing a legion of sales representatives in solar-friendly states across the country. Though most sales are generated through customer referrals, door-to-door sales became a significant means of reaching new customers over the last three years.

Most affected employees will be reassigned to other sales channels or given the opportunity to interview for other positions, Tesla said. About 1,000 people work in door-to-door sales for the company.

The company said it plans to expand its retail and online sales of solar systems, including in Tesla stores. It will also continue selling systems through long-standing partnerships with retailers, including Home Depot and Best Buy Co Inc .

"We expect the growth of these channels to end up more than offsetting the loss of door-to-door sales," Tesla said.

Tesla, which completed its acquisition of SolarCity in November, has repeatedly said that it would prioritize preserving cash over increasing sales of solar systems. It has also said that it would reduce the cost of acquiring new customers, a metric that has remained stubbornly high across the highly competitive industry.

In keeping with its move toward more distinctive solar offerings, Tesla has said it plans to roll out a line of solar roof tiles later this year. The solar-powered roof shingles were unveiled last October to showcase the benefits of combining Elon Musk's electric car maker with the solar installer.

(Reporting by Nichola Groom; Editing by Jonathan Oatis) ((nichola.groom@thomsonreuters.com;))

Keywords: TESLA SOLAR/Copyright (c) 2017 Thomson Reuters

Tesla recruiting engineers in Mexico for California plant - 路透新闻

{{20170428T210927.821+0000}}Tesla recruiting engineers in Mexico for California plantBy Alexandria Sage

SAN FRANCISCO, April 28 (Reuters) - Tesla Inc is recruiting engineers from Mexico to work on robotics and other automated equipment at its California factory, according to LinkedIn postings viewed by Reuters, part of a hiring push to ready the plant for mass production of the upcoming Model 3.

The electric vehicle maker, which prides itself on its "Made in America" credentials, aims to build 500,000 cars a year by 2018 at its plant in Fremont, California, south of San Francisco. That would be a six-fold increase from 2016.

A recruiting poster published on LinkedIn by Tesla's senior technical recruiter, David Johnson, listed 15 types of engineers the company would be seeking at a May 5-8 recruiting event in Monterrey, Mexico. (https://www.linkedin.com/feed/update/urn:li:activity:6261290896936042496/)

Tesla did not immediately respond to a request for comment on its Mexico hiring plans.

The Silicon Valley carmaker is under the gun to accelerate production and save money as it readies for volume production of the Model 3 in September. The company's future profitability hinges on its success, and high hopes for the mass-market vehicle have helped push Tesla shares up 47 percent since January. [nL1N1HU0BC]

Mexico boasts a substantial pool of educated manufacturing engineers, with 19 automotive plants owned by global automakers including General Motors Co , Ford Motor Co , Fiat Chrysler Automobiles and Volkswagen .

Tesla's Johnson wrote in a post that he hoped to interview manufacturing and mechanical engineers with experience in "Body in White" (BIW) manufacturing. That is the stage of assembly in which sheet metal components are welded together to make up the outer frame of the car.

"Check this out if you are interested to work with the most complex and automated equipment in our Fremont plant! We are looking for controls, robotic and weld engineers!" posted another Tesla employee, Dominik Knapp, on his LinkedIn page.

Tesla has been actively hiring in the past few months for assembly-line jobs at the Fremont plant. But finding manufacturing engineers, who are in even shorter supply than software engineers in Silicon Valley, is a tougher challenge. [nL2N1831NS]

Doug Patton, president of SAE International, a professional association of automotive engineers headquartered in Pennsylvania, said Tesla's search for engineers in Mexico underscored a dearth of talent in the industry.

"There are many more jobs than engineers, this is an engineering problem across the board," he said.

U.S. automakers and suppliers will sometimes bring employees from Mexican plants to the United States for short-term assignments, but Patton said he had not heard of any company recruiting on a "wholesale basis" as Tesla appeared to be doing.

Tesla's vice president of production, Peter Hochholdinger, has experience in Mexico, having been involved in the launch of Audi's high-tech plant in Puebla.

(Editing by Jonathan Weber and Matthew Lewis) ((alexandria.sage@thomsonreuters.com; Reuters Messaging: alexandria.sage@thomsonreuters.com@reuters.net))

Keywords: TESLA MEXICO/Copyright (c) 2017 Thomson Reuters

What to Watch in the Week Ahead and on Monday, May 1 - 路透新闻

{{20170428T190348.878+0000}}What to Watch in the Week Ahead and on Monday, May 1(The Day Ahead is an email and PDF publication that includes the day's major stories and events, analyses and other features. To receive The Day Ahead, Eikon users can register at [DAY/US]. Thomson One users can register at RT/DAY/US. All times in ET/GMT)

WEEK AHEAD

Apple Inc is expected to post its second straight quarter of revenue growth on Tuesday, buoyed by sales of its high-end smartphones, particularly the iPhone 7 Plus. Analysts will be keeping an eye on Apple's typically conservative June-quarter forecast, which takes into account the lull in spending just before the company launches its latest phone. Investors will also be expecting Apple to increase its buyback program and dividends.

On Tuesday, the U.S. Federal Reserve's Federal Open Market Committee's two-day meeting on interest rates will commence, with their decision announced on Wednesday. On Friday, Fed Vice Chair Stanley Fischer will speak before the Hoover Monetary Policy Conference in Stanford, California. At the same event later in the day, Chicago Fed President Charles Evans, Boston Fed President Eric Rosengren and St. Louis Fed President James Bullard will participate in a panel on, "The Structural Foundations of Monetary Policy". On the same day in New York, Federal Reserve Bank of San Francisco President John Williams is scheduled to speak before the Shadow Open Market Committee.

Attention shifts to next week's April employment report, manufacturing and services sector surveys for confirmation that a sharp slowdown in economic growth in the first quarter was an aberration. The Institute for Supply Management will likely report on Monday that its national manufacturing index slipped to 56.4 in April from a reading of 57.2 in March. Also on Monday, the Commerce Department is expected to report that consumer spending increased 0.3 percent in March after edging up 0.1 percent in February. On Wednesday, the ISM is likely to report that its non-manufacturing index increased to 55.8 in April from 55.2 in March. Data on Thursday from the Commerce Department is expected to show the trade deficit rose to $44.5 billion in March from $43.6 billion in February. Also on Thursday, the Labor Department is likely to report that productivity increased at a 0.2 percent annualized rate in the first quarter, after rising at a 1.3 percent pace in the fourth quarter. On Friday, the Labor Department's closely watched employment report is expected to show nonfarm payrolls increased 180,000 in April after rising 89,000 in March. The unemployment rate is forecast ticking up to 4.6 percent from 4.5 percent in March. Average hourly earnings are expected to have increased 0.3 percent after gaining 0.2 percent in March.

Social media giant Facebook Inc is expected to post a jump in first-quarter revenue on Wednesday. For the past few quarters Facebook's mobile-ad sales have been soaring, boosting its overall growth. However, the company warned in November that ad growth would likely slow "meaningfully" due to limits on "ad load." Chief Executive Mark Zuckerberg said in February that the company expects a major ramp-up in hiring and other spending during 2017 as it invests in video and other priorities.

Three of the largest U.S. insurers, American International Group Inc, MetLife Inc and Prudential Inc are scheduled to hold earnings calls to discuss results announced after the market closes on Wednesday. All eyes will be on AIG, whose board is hunting for a new CEO after a large 2016 fourth quarter loss roiled shareholders. First-quarter results will reveal the impact of an uptick in March catastrophe losses for property insurers, including AIG, which prompted at least one analyst to lower estimates for AIG and others. Prudential's and MetLife's report will show whether results align with analysts' rosy expectations for a strong quarter among life insurers.

MasterCard Inc, the world's No. 2 payments network, is expected to report a rise in revenue and profit on Tuesday, helped by higher purchase volumes. Investors would be interested in any guidance on the year ahead, including on expenses, as MasterCard has been focusing on digital growth.

Pfizer Inc is expected to post weaker first-quarter revenue before the bell on Tuesday, as the U.S. drugmaker's portfolio groans under the weight of looming patent expirations, as well as those that have already begun to chip away at sales. After deciding against splitting itself up last year, there will be considerable focus on Pfizer's traditionally voracious appetite for M&A as it looks to strengthen its ship, with chatter about Bristol-Myers' Squibb as a potential target doing the rounds. On the same day Merck & Co is scheduled to report first-quarter results. With the next frontier in cancer immunotherapy within reach, investors will be laser focused on the performance of Merck's Keytruda, after Bristol-Myers reported strong quarterly growth for rival drug Opdivo last week. Considered Merck's most significant growth driver, Wall Street is hoping for signs that Keytruda and other drugs in the company's pipeline will be enough to offset patent expirations on many key products.

Berkshire Hathaway Inc, the conglomerate run by billionaire Warren Buffett, is expected to report first-quarter results on Friday after U.S. markets close. The results are to be issued one day before Berkshire holds its annual shareholder meeting in Omaha, Nebraska. Buffett and Vice Chairman Charlie Munger are expected for five hours to answer questions from shareholders, investors and analysts on Saturday, the centerpiece of a weekend of events throughout the city.

Time Warner Inc, which is being bought by AT&T, is expected to report a rise in first-quarter revenue on Wednesday, helped by the success of its movies 'Kong' and 'The Lego Batman Movie' as well as higher cable revenues. In January, AT&T said it expected to be able to bypass the U.S. FCC in its planned $85.4 billion acquisition of Time Warner because it would not seek to transfer any significant Time Warner licenses.

Tesla Inc is scheduled to report first-quarter results on Wednesday after markets close. Shortly after, Chief Executive Elon Musk is scheduled to hold an investor call.

Mondelez International Inc's first quarter profit is likely to beat analysts' estimates on Tuesday, helped by cost cuts through its zero-based budgeting plan. Mondelez has targeted cost savings of 30-50 percent in 12 areas, including travel, sales support services and business events. Investors will look forward to the company's 2017 profit forecast to know the efficacy of its cost-cutting plan. Separately, Kraft Heinz Co's quarterly revenue growth is likely to have slowed as the company has been forced to adjust its products as shoppers increasingly shun packaged foods for fresher items and those perceived to be healthier. However, Kraft Heinz, reporting on Wednesday, has also been benefiting from lower prices of raw materials, including dairy products and coffee, which is likely to lift its quarterly profit. Investors will be looking forward to any news about the company's strategy in the near future and its 2017 profit and revenue forecasts as its bid to take over Anglo-Dutch company Unilever recently fell apart.

ConocoPhillips, the largest independent oil company in the United States, is expected to swing to a quarterly profit on Tuesday, helped by the rise in oil prices. Conoco has been selling assets to reduce its exposure to profit-sapping natural gas assets and to shore up its balance sheet. Investors will seek details of the company's plans to sell assets worth $17 billion to Cenovus Energy - a transaction that has irked investors of the Canadian company, who have complained that the deal price is too high. Oil and gas producer Anadarko Petroleum Corp is expected to post a smaller quarterly loss on Tuesday, buoyed by rising oil prices. The company set a higher capital budget for the year in March to focus on higher-margin oil production. Investors will seek details of the company's drilling plans for the year. Occidental Petroleum Corp is expected to report a smaller quarterly profit on Thursday as high costs outweigh gains from a rise in crude prices. Occidental, which has cut its budget for the year, has been focusing on Texas' prolific Permian basin. Analysts and investors seek details on the company's plans to reduce costs.

Humana Inc reports first-quarter earnings before the bell on Wednesday. The health insurer, which has pre-announced its first-quarter profit, is likely to benefit from strength in its Medicare Advantage business. Investors will watch out for comments about President Donald Trump's plan to revamp the U.S. healthcare system. Humana has said it would exit Obamacare business in 2018. Aetna Inc, the No. 3 U.S. health insurer, is scheduled to report its first-quarter earnings on Tuesday, followed by Cigna Corp on Friday, before the market opens. Cigna is also waiting for a decision from a federal appeals court, which had been asked to rule on whether the Justice Department could stop Cigna and Anthem Inc's $54 billion merger on antitrust grounds.

IT services provider Cognizant Technology Solutions Corp is expected to report a rise in first-quarter revenue on Friday. The company is benefiting a huge demand for its digital and cloud services. Investors and analysts would be looking out for Cognizant's comments on U.S. President Trump's tough stance on H1-B visa rules. About three-quarters of Cognizant's employees are in India.

CVS Health Corp, a drugstore chain and pharmacy benefits manager (PBM), lowered its full-year PBM unit revenue growth forecast, which analysts partly attributed to branded drug price increases coming in lower than anticipated. CVS said in March it had lost a contract to manage specialty drug benefits for the Federal Employee Program to Prime Therapeutics. Traffic in its stores is also expected to have been weak in the quarter. The company will report on Tuesday. Separately, drug wholesaler AmerisourceBergen Corp will report first-quarter earnings before the market opens on Thursday. Pharmaceutical supply chain, including pharmacy benefit managers and drug distributors, have been squeezed as a result of pricing pressure due to heightened scrutiny over drug price hikes. Investors will also focus on pricing commentary related to independent pharmacy networks.

Viacom Inc, the owner of MTV, Comedy Central and the Paramount film studio, is seen reporting a fall in quarterly profit on Thursday. The company has faced several quarters of declines in domestic advertising revenue as it grapples with shifting audience preferences. CEO Bakish is making Paramount a major part of his strategy to turn around the media conglomerate's declining ad revenue and ratings. Separately on the same day, CBS Corp, owner of the most widely-viewed U.S. television network, is expected to post a drop in first-quarter revenue, in part due to a strong year-ago quarter that benefited from the 2016 Super Bowl and political ad spend.

Yum Brands Inc's Pizza Hut chain is expected to continue its string of falling same-store sales, while rival Domino's reported a better-than-expected 14 percent jump in U.S. comparable sales. However, Taco Bell is expected to have benefited from promotions, while KFC is expected to have had steady growth. Yum Brands is scheduled to report its results on Wednesday. Dunkin Brands Group Inc, the owner of Dunkin' Donuts and Baskin Robbins, issued a conservative 2017 forecast in February, forecasting low single-digit comparable U.S. sales growth for both the chains. Dunkin' is streamlining its menus to speed up service, reducing waste and could potentially reduce staff turnover by making employees' work easier. The company is expected to report on Thursday. Sprint Corp is scheduled to report fourth-quarter results on Wednesday. The wireless carrier is expected to post a rise in profit as it benefits from revamped plans that offer unlimited data. Investors and analysts will be looking out for any comments on a potential deal with rival T-Mobile.

Akamai Technologies Inc is expected to report a rise in first-quarter revenue, driven by strong demand for its security services. However, Akamai has been experiencing continued slowdown in its media delivery business after some of its large customers shifted to their own delivery networks, and this could hurt the company's future revenue. The company is scheduled to report on Tuesday. On the same day, FireEye Inc is expected to report its second straight fall in quarterly revenue. The cybersecurity company has been struggling to regain momentum in a highly competitive market and is also coping with a string of executive departures. The company is also shifting to a subscription-based revenue model, which is expected to lead to more stable revenue streams in the future.

Kellogg Co, the world's largest maker of breakfast cereals, has seen its profits rise due to restructuring program, "Project K", launched to counter slowing sales as Americans choose healthier options over processed foods. Investors will look out for additional cost-cutting actions under the program. The company is expected to report first-quarter results on Thursday.

Regeneron Pharmaceuticals Inc, which is facing slowing sales of its blockbuster eye drug Eylea, is expected to report first-quarter results before the bell on Thursday. Investors will be looking for comments on company's potential blockbuster treatments Dupixent and Sarilumab, as the U.S. biotech reduces reliance on Eylea. Investors will also seek details on the company and partner Sanofi SA' patent war against Amgen Inc for its cholestrol drug Praluent and eczema treatment Dupixent. Separately on Tuesday, Gilead Sciences Inc, maker of HIV and hepatitis treatments, is scheduled to report first-quarter results.

Chesapeake Energy Corp, the second-largest U.S. natural gas producer, is expected to swing to a quarterly profit on Thursday, helped by improved oil and gas prices. Investors will look for an update on the company's plans to accelerate its debt reduction target of $2 billion-$3 billion over the next few years through additional asset sales. On the same day, Apache Corp is expected to swing to a quarterly profit, also bolstered by higher crude prices. The company set a higher spending target for 2017 earlier this year, encouraged by the price recovery. Investors will seek details on Apache's drilling plans for the year. Offshore drilling contractor Noble Corp Plc is expected to post a quarterly loss on Thursday, compared with a year-ago profit, as customer spending on expensive offshore projects remains weak. Investors will seek details of the company's order book and efforts to cut costs amid the prolonged slump in demand. On Tuesday, Devon Energy Corp is expected to report a first-quarter profit, compared with a year-ago loss, as rising oil prices boost cash flows. Investors will seek details of the company's drilling plans for the year.

HCA Holdings Inc, the largest U.S. for-profit hospital operator, reports first-quarter results before the bell on Tuesday. HCA, which pre-announced part of its results, is expected to report soft volumes due to weak hospital operating environment. Investors will watch out for comments on the likely impact of on hospital operators from the Trump administration's plan to overhaul the U.S. healthcare system.

Videogame publisher Activision Blizzard Inc is expected to report a rise in quarterly revenue and profit on Thursday, helped by higher digital downloads of its games and its acquisition of Candy Crush maker King Digital. Activision Blizzard recently unveiled the latest installment of its popular Call of Duty franchise, set around events in World War II and characters such as Nazi Zombies. After the disappointing performance of 2016's game, analysts and investors will be closely watching any commentary from Activision and player's responses to gauge how the game will be received when it releases in late 2017. Zynga Inc is expected to report a rise in quarterly revenue on Thursday, helped by its popular franchises including Zynga Poker and Words With Friends. Advertising revenue from its games in the period is expected to be typically lean, but analysts are looking beyond the quarter to see what Zynga's game slate for 2017 is like.

On Tuesday, agricultural trader Archer Daniels Midland will report first-quarter earnings amid abundant global grain stocks that have lowered costs for the raw materials it processes into vegetable oil, corn sweetener and ethanol. But the plentiful crop supplies have also squeezed trading margins and the company has been shedding traders around the world. Separately on Wednesday, Bunge Ltd will report first-quarter results. Investors will be watching for clues on crop marketing in Brazil and Argentina, where farmers are harvesting bumper corn and soy crops, as a large share of Bunge's assets are in South America.

First Solar Inc is expected to report a first-quarter loss on Tuesday, compared with a year-ago profit, as it transitions to a new product ahead of schedule. Solar companies have been struggling with a sharp decline in panel prices since mid-2016, but the company said in February that bookings had picked up since the end of last year. Analysts and investors will look for comments on panel pricing and demand.

On Wednesday, New York Times Co is expected to report a drop in first-quarter profit, hurt by higher operating costs. However, the magazine and newspaper publisher has been ramping up its digital business to offset its declining print sales.

On Tuesday, U.S.-based fertilizer maker Mosaic Co is expected to post a bigger first-quarter profit, as potash prices modestly rebound. Investors will be interested in any updates on Mosaic's acquisition of Vale's fertilizer assets. On Wednesday, U.S. nitrogen fertilizer producer CF Industries reports first-quarter results. Of interest to investors are the company's thoughts on new U.S. production coming online this year, which could weigh on prices.

Estee Lauder Cos Inc is scheduled to report third-quarter results on Wednesday. The cosmetics maker has been struggling with low mall traffic in the United States as shoppers increasingly prefer to buy personal products online. Investors will look out for comments on tourist spending, both within the U.S. and in major international markets. Handbag maker Coach Inc is expected to report a dip in third-quarter sales on the same day. The company has been battling rising competition and increased discounting. Coach, in a push to regain its premium tag, has tightened inventory and cut back on promotions in North America.

Fitbit Inc is expected to post its second straight fall in quarterly revenue on Wednesday as the fitness band maker grapples with waning demand for its fitness tracking bands in a maturing market. Analysts and investors will be on the looking out for a new product cycle.

Denver-based Molson Coors Brewing Co is expected to report a jump in quarterly sales and profit, helped by its $12 billion acquisition last year of the remaining 58 percent of MillerCoors from beer giant SABMiller. The deal made Molson Coors, known for its flagship Coors Light brew, the third-largest brewer in the world. A strong U.S. dollar, which is expected to stay strong, will likely have tempered earnings and investors will look for any currency impact down the line.

TransCanada Corp reports first-quarter results and holds its annual general meeting on Friday. Investors will be looking for updates on shipper commitments on its recently approved Keystone XL crude oil pipeline, which is still awaiting route approval in Nebraska.

Home Capital Group, Canada biggest non-bank lender, is scheduled to report first-quarter results on Wednesday. On Thursday, Ontario's financial regulator hears a case against the company, whose shares fell 50 percent and which is looking at strategic options. The case relates to allegations that some of the lender's current and former executives failed to meet continuous disclosure obligations relating to its termination of certain broker partners it had found engaged in fraud.

SNC Lavalin Group Ltd, a Canadian engineering and construction company, is expected to report a bigger profit on Thursday, as it won contracts. Investors will seek an update on the company's recently announced acquisition of British construction company WS Atkins for C$3.6 billion.

On Friday, Air Canada Inc is expected to report a quarterly loss, compared with a year-ago profit, hurt by a rise in costs. Investors will seek details of its plans to upgrade its fleet with fuel-efficient aircraft.

Encana Corp, Canada's No. 2 oil and natural gas producer, is expected to swing to a quarterly profit, helped by higher oil prices. Investors will look for details on the company's drilling plans for the year when it reports on Tuesday. In recent years Encana has narrowed operations to focus on four core North American plays: the Montney and Duvernay in Western Canada, and the Eagle Ford and Permian in the United States. Separately, Husky Energy Inc is expected to post a quarterly profit on Friday, compared with a year-ago loss, as it sells more crude oil at higher prices. Investors will seek details on the company's drilling plans for the year.

Loblaw Companies Ltd, a Canadian grocery and pharmacy retailer, is expected to report a higher first-quarter profit on Wednesday as its cost-cutting efforts pay off. The company has been streamlining operations to counter intense competition from U.S. discount stores and ecommerce companies. Analysts and investors will look for comments on pricing and further cost cuts.

Torstar Corp, the owner of one of Canada's largest circulation daily newspapers, is expected to post a smaller first-quarter loss on Wednesday as a growing digital business offsets declines in its print ads. Torstar's plans to grow its digital business will be of interest to investors.

Canadian gold miner Kinross Gold Corp is expected to report flat earnings on Tuesday, which is likely to include a gain from the recent sale of its stake in the Cerro Casale project in Chile. Investors are likely to focus on the potential sale of the company's Chilean assets and whether it is leaning toward going ahead with the second phase of expansion of its Tasiast mine in Mauritania. A decision on that is expected in the third quarter.

Shopify Inc, a Canadian ecommerce software maker, is expected to post a bigger quarterly loss on Tuesday as operating expenses rise.

Canada's jobs report for April will be released on Friday, as will a separate report on Ivey PMI. Investors will also get a look at the trade balance report for March on Thursday.

Bank of Canada Governor Stephen Poloz will give a speech in Mexico City on Thursday. The central bank head is likely to be pressed about the potential economic ramifications of altering or scrapping the North American Free Trade Agreement.

On Tuesday, Mexico Markit PMI data will be released for April, the month after factory activity rose to its highest level this year. On Thursday, Mexico will publish gross fixed investment data for February.

ON MONDAY - MAY 1

A busy economic calendar kick starts the week with several economic indicators scheduled for release. The Institute for Supply Management releases its manufacturing index for April which is expected to show a slightly lower reading of 56.4. (1000/1400) Markit Manufacturing PMI final figures for April are expected. (0945/1345) The Commerce Department will release personal income figures for March, which likely rose at a lower 0.3 percent rate from 0.4 percent in February. (0830/1230) Monthly core PCE Price Index data for March is expected to dip 0.1 percent. (0830/1230) March construction spending likely rose at a slower 0.4 percent compared to a month earlier. (1000/1400)

Chipmaker Advanced Micro Devices is expected to report its fourth straight quarter of revenue growth. Analysts expects AMD's new line of Ryzen processors to finally grab market share from Intel in the desktop, notebook and server market this year. AMD's low-end graphics chips have also been performing strongly, putting the company in a stronger position to compete against Nvidia.

Satellite TV provider Dish Network Corp is expected to report a rise in quarterly profit helped by new additions to its Sling TV streaming service. The company is a prime target for M&A as the FCC is about to remove the ban on telecom companies engaging in merger talks.

Cardinal Health will report its third-quarter results before the market opens. The results come a week after the drug distributor said it would buy Medtronic Plc's medical supplies units for $6.1 billion to add heft to its growing medical products business. The move was, however, overshadowed by the company's dour forecast, underscoring the U.S. drug distribution industry's struggles with declining generic drug prices.

Debt-laden hospital operators Community Health and Tenet Healthcare will report first-quarter results after market close. Both companies are likely to report soft patient volumes and investors will watch out for comments on President Donald Trump's plan to repeal and replace the Affordable Care Act, popularly known as Obamacare. Hospitals have benefited from Obamacare's expansion of insurance coverage.

Offshore drilling contractor Diamond Offshore is expected to post a quarterly loss, compared with a year-ago profit, as customer spending on expensive offshore projects remains weak. Investors will seek details on the company's order book and efforts to cut costs amid the prolonged slump in demand.

Canadian fertilizer maker Agrium Inc will report first-quarter results, ahead of an expected merger mid-year with Potash Corp of Saskatchewan. Investors will be keen for updates on applications for merger approval from regulators.

Canada's seasonally adjusted manufacturing PMI data for April is expected. (0930/1330)

(Compiled by Nandi Kaul in Bangalore; Editing by Savio D'Souza) ((Nandi.Kaul@thomsonreuters.com;))

REFILE--In first 100 days, a reversal of fortune for Trump favorites on Wall Street - 路透新闻

{{20170428T185929.485+0000}}REFILE--In first 100 days, a reversal of fortune for Trump favorites on Wall Street(Fixes link to Factbox on sector performance)

By Noel Randewich

SAN FRANCISCO, April 28 (Reuters) - A funny thing happened on Wall Street in Donald Trump's first 100 days in the White House: Shares of companies that got closest to the president lagged the market's march higher.

Meanwhile, stocks from sectors that have had less access, and have faced occasional bluster from Trump, such as media and technology, have hopped into the driver seat.

Banks, industrials and other companies expected to win from Trump's policies surged following his unexpected election victory in November. Valuations for many grew stretched.

But Wall Street's change in focus in recent months also reflects concerns among investors that Trump may struggle to enact deep tax cuts and stimulate economic growth as quickly as previously expected. Indeed, the economy grew just 0.7 percent on an annualized basis in the first quarter, the first of Trump's presidency, as consumer spending stalled. [nL1N1HY232]

Many of the industries Trump singled out for special attention, like coalminers, steelmakers and oil companies, face major market trends and commodity price fluctuations that he can do little to change.

Since Trump's inauguration on Jan. 20, representatives from nearly 100 publicly-listed companies have visited the White House, with carmakers, healthcare companies, banks and industrials getting more face time than technology companies, retailers and media firms. [nL1N1HX0WV]

Shares of companies that have visited the White House since the inauguration have enjoyed a median increase of 3.7 percent, trailing the benchmark Standard & Poor's 500 Index's gain of 5.5 percent.

But Trump's recent failure to push a healthcare overhaul through Congress, as well as other miscues, now have investors a little less sure he will be able to make good on his promises.

The S&P 500 is near record highs after the administration unveiled a long-awaited proposal Wednesday to steeply cut corporate tax rates. But the plan may be unpalatable to Republican fiscal hawks since it lacks proposals for raising new revenue and would potentially add billions of dollars to the federal deficit.

"The stability of the market and its ability to rise is still based on the feeling that the administration may be getting its act together," said Tim Ghriskey, chief investment officer of Solaris Group in Bedford Hills, New York. "But at some point investors will ask if any of this stuff is going to happen or if it's all talk."

EARLY WINNERS FADE

Since the election, the financial sector <.SPSY> has risen 19 percent, more than any other. But its gain since the inauguration has been among the weakest, at 3 percent.

An investor buying a basket of banks and selling utilities immediately after Trump's election would have made as much as 29 percent by mid-February. But that gain has since shrunk to 17 percent, according to Vincent Deluard, Vice President, Global Macro Strategy at INTL FCStone Financial Inc.

Other "Trump trades" have lost momentum.

Investors bet big on steel right out of the gate after Election Day, with the industry seen as a poster child for Trump's focus on "unfair" trade deals that hurt U.S. producers. The S&P 1500 steel industry group index <.SPCOMSTEEL> had gained 36 percent by the first week of December.

The group is down by more than 13 percent since then, however, and even last week's executive order to investigate whether U.S. steel companies need additional trade protections under the auspices of national security delivered only a short-lived rebound. Poor earnings from sector heavyweight United States Steel Corp ruined the party.

Trump this month signed an executive order sweeping away Obama-era climate change regulations, saying it would end America's "war on coal." But reflecting an abundance of cheap natural gas and falling costs of wind and solar power, coal miners CONSOL Energy and Cloud Peak Energy have dropped 16 percent and 32 percent, respectively, in Trump's first 100 days. [nL5N1HC3E3]

Meanwhile, tech stocks that were left out of the early Trump rally have surged recently as investors shift out of low-valuation stocks favored immediately after the election and back into high-growth stocks like Alphabet and Facebook that delivered much of the market's momentum in recent years.

In the absence of concrete results from Trump, corporate earnings have taken center stage, with first-quarter profits of S&P 500 companies expected to surge 13.6 percent, helped by strong international growth.

"Earnings are through-the-roof good. Companies are very profitable, and potentially are going to be more profitable with tax-cut legislation," said Stephen Massocca, Senior Vice President at Wedbush Securities in San Francisco.

Other stocks seen as out of favor under Trump have also outperformed during his first 100 days.

Tesla , which some investors feared could be hurt by the removal of tax incentives for the purchase of its electric vehicles, has surged 27 percent to record highs.

And perhaps most telling of all, the media sector - regularly lambasted by Trump for its coverage of him - is up 7 percent since he took office.

Even New York Times Co , publisher of what Trump has repeatedly disparaged as "the failed New York Times" newspaper, hit a three-year high after the inauguration and is up 10 percent since he moved into the White House.

Apple asks California to change its proposed self-driving car testing policies - 路透新闻

{{20170428T180152.481+0000}}Apple asks California to change its proposed self-driving car testing policiesApril 28 (Reuters) - Apple Inc asked the state of California to make changes in its proposed self-driving car policies, the latest sign the company is pursuing driverless car technology.

In a letter made public Friday, Apple made a series of suggested changes to the policy that is under development and said it looks forward to working with California and others "so that rapid technology development may be realized while ensuring the safety of the traveling public."

Alphabet Inc's self-driving car unit Waymo , Ford Motor Co , Uber Technologies Inc [UBER.UL], Toyota Motor Corp <7203.T>, Tesla Motors Inc and others also filed comments suggesting changes.

Guten Morgen von Reuters am Freitag, den 28. April - 路透新闻

{{20170428T045829.517+0000}}Guten Morgen von Reuters am Freitag, den 28. AprilTOP NEWS:

* NORDKOREA: US-Präsident Trump hat vor einer Eskalation im Nordkorea-Konflikt gewarnt. "Am
liebsten würden wir diese Dinge diplomatisch lösen, aber das ist sehr schwierig", sagte er in
einem Interview mit der Nachrichtenagentur Reuters. Es bestehe absolut die Möglichkeit, dass es
am Ende zu einem großen Konflikt mit Nordkorea komme. Unterdessen hat China Nordkorea laut
US-Angaben eindringlich vor einem neuen Atomwaffentest gewarnt. Die Regierung in Peking habe
Nordkorea deutlich gemacht, dass sie Sanktionen verhängen werde, sollte das abgeschottete Land
abermals einen Nuklearsprengkopf testen, sagte US-Außenminister Tillerson dem Sender Fox News.

* GROSSBRITANNIEN: Die britische Polizei hat bei einem Anti-Terror-Einsatz in London und dem
nahe gelegen Kent vier Verdächtige festgenommen. Zudem sei eine Frau angeschossen worden,
teilten die Sicherheitsbehörden mit. Die vier Festgenommenen stünden unter Verdacht der
Anstiftung und Vorbereitung einer Terrortat.

* AMAZON: Der Expansionskurs des weltgrößten Online-Händlers zahlt sich aus. Dank
des anhaltenden Wachstums der Online-Verkäufe und des Cloud-Geschäfts stiegen Gewinn und Umsatz
im ersten Quartal überraschend kräftig. Das Nettoergebnis kletterte binnen Jahresfrist um 41
Prozent auf 724 Millionen Dollar. Der Umsatz stieg um 23 Prozent auf 35,7 Milliarden Dollar.

* MICROSOFT: Der US-Softwareriese profitiert kräftig vom boomenden Cloud-Geschäft.
Der Quartalsgewinn kletterte deswegen um 28 Prozent auf 4,8 Milliarden Dollar. Der Umsatz stieg
um sechs Prozent auf 23,56 Milliarden Dollar, verfehlte aber knapp die Erwartungen. Hier macht
dem Konzern der harte Konkurrenzkampf im PC-Geschäft zu schaffen. Die Einnahmen mit Laptops und
Tablets der Marke Surface brachen um gut ein Viertel ein.

* ALPHABET: Ein boomendes Werbegeschäft auf Smartphones und Tablets füllt dem
Internet-Riesen die Kassen. Der Mutterkonzern Alphabet wies einen Umsatzsprung von rund 22
Prozent auf 24,75 Milliarden Dollar im ersten Quartal aus. Der Nettogewinn kletterte sogar
überraschend kräftig um 29 Prozent auf 5,4 Milliarden Dollar. Dabei zahlt sich auch der Fokus
auf die Video-Tochter YouTube aus.

FIRMEN UND BRANCHEN - WEITERE NACHRICHTEN UND TERMINE:

* INTEL: Der weltgrößte Chiphersteller hat im vergangenen Quartal dank eines sich
stabilisierenden PC-Marktes und Zuwächsen im Geschäft mit Datenzentren Gewinn und Umsatz
gesteigert. Der Überschuss sprang in den ersten drei Monaten verglichen mit demselben
Vorjahreszeitraum um 45 Prozent auf 2,96 Milliarden Dollar.

* UNITED AIRLINES: Die US-Fluggesellschaft hat mit einem gewaltsam aus einer Maschine
geworfenen Passagier einen Vergleich geschlossen. Es sei eine gütliche Einigung erzielt worden,
teilte das Unternehmen mit.

* FACEBOOK will verstärkt gegen Falschmeldungen und anderen Missbrauch vorgehen. So
sollten gefälschte Konten durch den Einsatz von intelligenter Software und Analysen wie bei
Geheimdiensten erkannt und dann gesperrt oder gelöscht werden.

* RENAULT hat im ersten Quartal dank neuer Pkw-Modelle einen Umsatzsprung erzielt.
Die Erlöse kletterten um 25,2 Prozent auf 13,13 Milliarden Euro. Die Franzosen steigerten
demnach ihre Verkäufe und Marktanteile in allen Regionen.

* OMV: Der österreichische Öl- und Gaskonzern hat im ersten Quartal einen
überraschend starken Gewinnsprung erzielt. Das Nettoergebnis (CCS Überschuss) schoss in die Höhe
auf rund 500 (Vorjahreszeitraum: 174) Millionen Euro.

* ALITALIA[CAITLA.UL]: Die Regierung in Rom zeigt kein Interesse, die schwer angeschlagene
Fluglinie zu retten. Der Staat sei nicht bereit, sich direkt oder indirekt an einer
Kapitalerhöhung zu beteiligen, sagte Italiens Wirtschaftsminister Padoan.

* AMERICAN AIRLINES hat nach eigenen Angaben die Auslieferungstermine für mehrere
Langstreckenflugzeuge von AIRBUS und BOEING aufgeschoben.

* TESLA: Klaus Grohmann, früherer Chef des vom Elektroautobauer Tesla übernommenen
Maschinenbauers Grohmann, hat Insidern zufolge nach einem Zwist mit dem neuen US-Eigner seinen 
Posten abgegeben. Grohmann habe sich mit Tesla-Chef Musk überworfen, sagten mehrere mit dem
Vorgang vertraute Personen der Nachrichtenagentur Reuters. "Ich bin sicherlich nicht
ausgeschieden, weil ich keine Lust mehr habe", sagte Grohmann. Weiter wollte er sich nicht zu
den Umständen seinen Abgangs äußern.

ausgetauscht werden können.

Guten Abend von Reuters am Donnerstag, den 27. April - 路透新闻

{{20170427T163303.281+0000}}Guten Abend von Reuters am Donnerstag, den 27. AprilTOP NEWS:

* EZB: Die Europäische Zentralbank rückt von ihrem Kurs der weit offenen Geldschleusen trotz
verbesserter Wirtschaftsaussichten nicht ab. Zwar bestätigten Konjunkturdaten seit Anfang März,
dass die Erholung zunehmend solider werde und die Gefahren gesunken seien, sagte EZB-Chef
Draghi. "Ein erhebliches Ausmaß an geldpolitischer Unterstützung ist immer noch nötig",
schränkte der Italiener aber ein. Es brauche sehr günstige Finanzierungsbedingungen, um die
Inflation in Richtung des EZB-Ziels von knapp unter zwei Prozent zu treiben. Ein Ausstieg aus
den Konjunkturhilfen sei auf dem Ratstreffen der Notenbank nicht diskutiert worden.

* Die DEUTSCHE BANK arbeitet sich in kleinen Schritten aus der Krise. Weil der
wichtige Anleihehandel zu Jahresbeginn gut lief und die Vermögensverwaltung neue Gelder
einsammelte, zog der Gewinn stärker an, als Analysten zu hoffen gewagt hatten. Unter dem Strich
verdiente Deutschlands größtes Geldhaus im ersten Quartal 575 Millionen Euro - mehr als doppelt
so viel wie vor einem Jahr. Von den alten Glanzzeiten ist das Institut aber weit entfernt, denn
auch vor Steuern reichte es nicht zum Milliardengewinn.

* Die DEUTSCHE BÖRSE will nach dem gescheiterten Zusammenschluss mit der LONDON
STOCK EXCHANGE (LSE) künftig die Finger von solchen Deals lassen. "Wir haben gelernt,
dass Konsolidierung im Kerngeschäft der Börsen etwas schwierig ist und politisch nicht
unterstützt wird", sagte Deutsche-Börse-Finanzchef Pottmeyer. Deshalb müsse sich der Konzern in
anderen Bereichen nach Zukaufsmöglichkeiten umsehen - etwa im Geschäft mit Indizes, Währungen
und Rohstoffen.

* BUNDESWEHR/TERRORVERDACHT: Die Polizei hat im bayerischen Hammelburg einen 28-jährigen
Bundeswehr-Soldaten wegen des Verdachts auf Anschlagsplanungen festgenommen. Dem Oberleutnant
werde vorgeworfen, Ende Januar auf dem Wiener Flughafen Schwechat eine geladene Pistole in einem
Putzschacht in einer Toilette versteckt zu haben, teilte die Staatsanwaltschaft Frankfurt am
Donnerstag mit. Ein konkretes Anschlagsziel sei allerdings nicht bekannt.

* MÄRKTE: Nach dem Rekordlauf der vergangenen Tage ist der Aktienbörse am Donnerstag die
Puste ausgegangen. Selbst die Aussicht auf weiterhin niedrige Euro-Leitzinsen und zahlreiche
Quartalsbilanzen dies- und jenseits des Atlantiks überzeugten Anleger nicht. Die Steuerpläne von
US-Präsident Trump sorgten zusätzlich für Unsicherheit. Der Dax<.GDAXI> ging erstmals seit über
einer Woche mit Kursverlusten aus dem Handel, er gab 0,2 Prozent auf 12.443,79 Punkte nach. Der
EuroStoxx<.STOXX50E> verlor 0,4 Prozent auf 3563,29 Zähler. An der Wall Street lag der
Dow-Jones-Standardwerteindex<.DJI> zu Börsenschluss in Europa ebenfalls im Minus.

=========================================

FIRMEN UND BRANCHEN:

DAX:

* Die LUFTHANSA hat Spekulationen um eine mögliche Übernahme der schwer
angeschlagenen Fluglinie ALITALIA[CAITLA.UL] eine Absage erteilt. Man sei an einem Kauf des
italienischen Rivalen nicht interessiert, sagte Finanzchef Svensson. "Wir sind nicht da, um
Alitalia zu kaufen." Eine italienische Zeitung hatte die Lufthansa als Retter für die einstige
Staats-Airline ins Spiel gebracht.

* BAYER: Im Countdown zur milliardenschweren Übernahme des US-Saatgutriesen
MONSANTO glänzt beim Pharma- und Chemiekonzern das Geschäft mit rezeptpflichtigen
Medikamenten. Vor allem Verkaufsschlager wie das Mittel Xarelto zur Vorbeugung von
Schlaganfällen ließen zum Jahresauftakt in Leverkusen die Kassen klingeln.

* RWE: Der neue Chef Schmitz hält trotz der zunehmenden Kritik von Umweltschützern
an den als besonders klimaschädlich geltenden Braunkohlekraftwerken des Konzerns fest. "Die
Braunkohle ist und bleibt ein wichtiger Faktor für bezahlbare und sichere Energie", betonte der
Manager auf der Hauptversammlung in Essen. Die Anlagen würden wie auch Steinkohle- oder
Gaskraftwerke gebraucht, um den schwankenden Ökostrom abzusichern. Allen Bemühungen zum Trotz
werde der Stromverbrauch weiter steigen. "Strom ist ein Wachstumsmarkt."

* BASF: Ein starkes Geschäft mit Basischemikalien sowie die anhaltende Erholung im
Öl- und Gasgeschäft geben BASF Schwung. Der weltgrößte Chemiekonzern baute seinen Gewinn im
ersten Quartal deutlich aus und ist nun etwas optimistischer für das Gesamtjahr.

* DAIMLER muss im Rechtsstreit über Werbung für ein angeblich emissionsarmes
Dieselauto Details seiner Technik zur Abgasbehandlung offen legen. Das ordnete das Landgericht
Stuttgart in der Verhandlung über die Klage der Deutschen Umwelthilfe (DUH) gegen den Autobauer
an.

Termine morgen:

* LINDE: Q1

* CONTINENTAL: HV mit Eckdaten zu Q1 - Analysten erwarten Q1 bereinigtes Ebit 1,14
Mrd Euro, Umsatz 10,56 Mrd Euro

MDAX:

* AIRBUS: Dem Flugzeugbauer sind im ersten Quartal die Aufträge überraschend stark
weggebrochen. Während der Umsatz binnen Jahresfrist noch um sieben Prozent auf 13 Milliarden
Euro zulegte, sackte das Volumen der neuen Bestellungen um fast die Hälfte auf 3,8 Milliarden
Euro ab, wie der Konzern am Donnerstag mitteilte. AMERICAN AIRLINES hat nach eigenen
Angaben die Auslieferungstermine für mehrere Langstreckenflugzeuge von AIRBUS und
BOEING aufgeschoben.

* RIB SOFTWARE: Q1

SDAX:

* GRAMMER: Der Autozulieferer warnt trotz zuletzt guter Geschäfte vor
existenzbedrohenden Folgen des Machtkampfs mit der Unternehmerfamilie Hastor. Die
Auftragseingänge aus der Autobranche seien von dem Einstieg der Bosnier als Großaktionär spürbar
belastet, erklärte Grammer am Donnerstag, bekräftigte aber angesichts eines sprudelnden
Quartalsgewinns seine Jahresprognose.

Termine morgen:

* WCM: Geschäftsbericht 2016

FIRMEN UND BRANCHEN - WEITERE NACHRICHTEN UND TERMINE:

* TESLA: Klaus Grohmann, früherer Chef des vom Elektroautobauer Tesla übernommenen
Maschinenbauers Grohmann, ist Insidern zufolge nach einem Zwist mit dem neuen US-Eigner von
seinem Posten abgetreten. Grohmann habe sich mit Tesla-Chef Musk überworfen, sagten mehrere mit
dem Vorgang vertraute Personen der Nachrichtenagentur Reuters. Grohmann habe nicht mit
Forderungen Musks übereingestimmt, sich zum Nachteil bisheriger Stammkunden wie
DAIMLER, BMW, INTEL und BOSCH[ROBG.UL] auf Tesla-Projekte zu
konzentrieren. Tesla habe den Manager nach der Übernahme des deutschen Unternehmens eigentlich
behalten wollen - und auch Grohmann habe bleiben wollen. Dies habe sich nun aber erledigt. "Ich
bin sicherlich nicht ausgeschieden, weil ich keine Lust mehr habe", sagte Grohmann. Weiter
wollte er sich nicht zu den Umständen seinen Abgangs äußern.

* FORD will nach einem schwierigen Quartal wieder Fahrt aufnehmen. Der zweitgrößte
US-Autobauer kündigte eine Stabilisierung der Gewinne im Jahresverlauf an. Im abgelaufenen
Vierteljahr brach der Überschuss um 36 Prozent ein auf 1,6 Milliarden Dollar. Neben einem
leichten Absatzrückgang trugen dazu vor allem gestiegene Kosten bei.

* BANKENABGABE: Die Gesamtsumme der für 2016 erhobenen Bankenabgabe habe 1,77 Milliarden
Euro betragen, heißt es laut "Handelsblatt" in einem Bericht des Bundesfinanzministeriums an den
Haushaltsausschuss des Bundestages. Damit hätten die Beiträge einen Rekordwert erreicht. Im Jahr
2015 mussten die deutschen Institute 1,58 Milliarden Euro zahlen.

BLICKPUNKT ZENTRALBANKEN UND KONJUNKTUR:

* DEUTSCHLAND/INFLATION: Die Inflation in Deutschland ist im April einen Tick stärker
gestiegen als erwartet. Vor allem teurere Reisen über Ostern sorgten dafür, dass die
Verbraucherpreise im Schnitt 2,0 Prozent über dem Niveau vor einem Jahr lagen, wie das
Statistische Bundesamt mitteilte. Ökonomen hatten nur mit 1,9 Prozent gerechnet.

* USA/KONJUNKTUR: Die US-Industrie hat im März den dritten Monat in Folge eine höhere
Nachfrage verbucht. Die Aufträge für langlebige Güter - also vom Flugzeug bis zum Toaster -
stiegen allerdings mit 0,7 Prozent zum Vormonat etwas schwächer als erwartet, wie das
Handelsministerium mitteilte. Von Reuters befragte Ökonomen hatten mit einem Plus von 1,2
Prozent gerechnet.

* In IRLAND bekommt der boomende Tourismus die Folgen des Brexit-Votums zu spüren. Die Zahl
der Besucher stieg zwischen Januar und März binnen Jahresfrist nur noch um 0,6 Prozent, wie das
irische Statistikamt mitteilte.

Termine morgen:

Jordan, "Erläuterungen zur Geld- und Anlagepolitik der Nationalbank" (10.00)

* FED: Rede des Präsidenten der Fed von Philadelphia, Harker, zum Thema "Wie MINT dich
überall hinbringen" auf dem X-STEM Symposium des US-Verteidigungsministeriums (20.30)

BLICKPUNKT POLITIK:

* EU/BREXIT: Bundeskanzlerin Merkel hat Großbritannien vor Illusionen bei den anstehenden
Brexit-Verhandlungen gewarnt. Großbritannien werde nach dem EU-Austritt als Drittstaat nicht
mehr über die gleichen Rechte verfügen wie bisher oder gar bessergestellt werden, sagte Merkel
in einer Regierungserklärung zum bevorstehenden EU-Spitzentreffen. Die EU-Unterhändler für die
Brexit-Gespräche demonstrierten bei einem Treffen in Luxemburg Geschlossenheit. "Wir sind einig,
wir haben eine klare Linie und wir sind bereit", sagte EU-Chefunterhändler Barnier.

* STEUERFLUCHT: Bundesfinanzminister Schäuble hat im Falle eines Wahlsieges der Union
weitere Schritte gegen Steuerflucht ins Ausland angekündigt. "Der Kampf gegen
Steuerhinterziehung und exzessive Steuervermeidung wird ein immerwährender Kampf sein", sagte
der CDU-Politiker. Er könne nur international erfolgreich sein. Der Bundestag verabschiedete mit
großer Mehrheit zwei Gesetze, mit denen die Koalition Konsequenzen aus dem Skandal um die Panama
Papers und der Gewinnverlagerung von Konzernen zieht.

* DEUTSCHLAND/SICHERHEIT: Gefährliche Islamisten können künftig mit elektronischen
Fußfesseln überwacht werden. Der Bundestag verabschiedete eine entsprechende Änderung des
BKA-Gesetzes.

* DEUTSCHLAND/SICHERHEIT: Angriffe auf Polizisten und Rettungskräfte werden in Zukunft
strenger geahndet. Der Bundestag stimmte für einen Gesetzentwurf von Justizminister Maas, mit
dem ein neuer Straftatbestand des tätlichen Angriffs auf Vollstreckungsbeamte eingeführt wird.

* EU/LIBYEN: In der Europäischen Union gibt es Zweifel an der Loyalität der libyschen
Küstenwache, die zentraler Bestandteil im Kampf gegen Schleuserbanden auf dem Mittelmeer werden
soll. Beim Treffen der EU-Verteidigungsminister in Malta wurde Kritik an Forderungen der
UN-gestützten Regierung in Tripolis zur Ausrüstung von Sicherheitskräften laut.

Insider - Grohmann-Chef nach Streit mit Tesla-CEO ausgeschieden - 路透新闻

{{20170427T162647.622+0000}}Insider - Grohmann-Chef nach Streit mit Tesla-CEO ausgeschiedenDüsseldorf, 27. Apr (Reuters) - Klaus Grohmann, früherer Chef des vom Elektroautobauer Tesla übernommenen Maschinenbauers Grohmann, ist Insidern zufolge nach einem Zwist mit dem neuen US-Eigner von seinem Posten abgetreten. Grohmann habe sich mit Tesla-Chef Elon Musk überworfen, sagten mehrere mit dem Vorgang vertraute Personen am Donnerstag der Nachrichtenagentur Reuters. Grohmann habe nicht mit Forderungen Musks übereingestimmt, sich zum Nachteil bisheriger Stammkunden wie Daimler, BMW, Intel und Bosch[ROBG.UL] auf Tesla-Projekte zu konzentrieren. Tesla habe den Manager nach der Übernahme des deutschen Unternehmens eigentlich behalten wollen - und auch Grohmann habe bleiben wollen. Dies habe sich nun aber erledigt. "Ich bin sicherlich nicht ausgeschieden, weil ich keine Lust mehr habe", sagte Grohmann. Weiter wollte er sich nicht zu den Umständen seinen Abgangs äußern.

Ein Tesla-Sprecher sagte zum Rückzug Grohmanns, der Unternehmer habe eine "einzigartige Firma" aufgebaut. Der 75-Jährige habe sich entschieden, mit den Amerikanern zusammenzuarbeiten, um seinen Rückzug aus dem Unternehmen vorzubereiten. Angesichts der Konzentration auf Tesla-Projekte habe man gemeinsam entschieden, dass jetzt der richtige Zeitpunkt für einen Generationswechsel gekommen sei.

Tesla hatte Grohmann im vergangenen Jahr übernommen und will den Anlagenbauer aus der Eifel zu einem Zentrum für automatisierte Fertigung ausbauen. Grohmann entwickelt und vertreibt entsprechende Anlagen, die Tesla für den Wandel zu einem Massenhersteller dringend benötigt. Noch in diesem Jahr soll der Verkauf des Mittelklassewagens Model 3 starten, die Produktion soll im Juli anlaufen. Bei den Plänen von Milliardär Musk für Teslas Aufstieg zu einem Volumenhersteller spielt das Model 3 eine zentrale Rolle. Seine Pläne für Grohmann hätten sich nicht verändert, sagten die Insider weiter. Die Management-Ebene unter Grohmann sei weiter an Bord.

Grohmanns Abgang hatte indes für Verunsicherung unter den Arbeitnehmern gesorgt. "Im November wurde uns noch gesagt, es bleibe alles beim Alten. Ende März waren wir überrascht zu hören, dass er in Ruhestand geht", hatte Betriebsratschef Uwe Herzig gesagt. Die IG Metall stritt zudem mit Tesla um die Einführung eines Tarifvertrags, dieser Zwist schien zuletzt aber entschärft.[nL8N1HY40C]

(Reporter: Edward Taylor, bearbeitet von Matthias Inverardi und Hans Seidenstücker; redigiert von Olaf Brenner. Bei Rückfragen wenden Sie sich an die Redaktionsleitung unter den Telefonnummern 069-7565 1232 oder 030-2888 5168) ((matthias.inverardi@thomsonreuters.com; +49 211 3882242; Reuters Messaging: matthias.inverardi.thomsonreuters.com@reuters.net www.twitter.com/REUTERS_DE www.reuters.de))Copyright (c) 2017 Thomson Reuters

EXCLUSIVE-Tesla's Klaus Grohmann ousted after clash with CEO Musk -sources - 路透新闻

{{20170427T162549.995+0000}}EXCLUSIVE-Tesla's Klaus Grohmann ousted after clash with CEO Musk -sourcesBy Edward Taylor

FRANKFURT, April 27 (Reuters) - Tesla executive Klaus Grohmann was ousted last month after a clash with Chief Executive Elon Musk over the strategy of Grohmann's firm, which Tesla had acquired in November, a source familiar with the matter told Reuters.

The Silicon Valley luxury electric carmaker is counting on Grohmann Engineering's automation and engineering expertise to help it ramp up production to 500,000 cars per year by 2018.

At the time of the purchase, it described Klaus Grohmann and the company he founded as a "world leader in highly automated manufacturing". [nL4N1D93YX]

Tesla planned to keep Grohmann on, and Grohmann wanted to stay, but the clash with Musk over how to treat existing clients resulted in his departure, the source said.

Grohmann disagreed with Musk's demands to focus management attention on Tesla projects to the detriment of Grohmann Engineering's legacy clients, which included Tesla's direct German-based rivals Daimler and BMW , two sources familiar with the matter said.

Reached by phone, Klaus Grohmann declined to comment on the circumstances of his leaving, citing confidentiality clauses.

"I definitely did not depart because I had lost interest in working," Grohmann said, without elaborating.

A Tesla spokesman, asked about Grohmann's departure, praised him for building an "incredible company" and said:

"Part of Mr Grohmann's decision to work with Tesla was to prepare for his retirement and leave the company in capable hands for the future. Given the change in focus to Tesla projects, we mutually decided that it was the right time for the next generation of management to lead."

Two sources familiar with the matter said Tesla's plans to ramp up production with the help of the company now renamed Tesla Grohmann Automation remain on track.

The management layer below Klaus Grohmann is continuing his work, they told Reuters. But they said parts of the workforce felt insecure about becoming so dependent on one client after the founder's departure.

Last year, Tesla had said: "Under the continued leadership of Mr Grohmann, several critical elements of Tesla's automated manufacturing systems will be designed and produced in Pruem, to help make our factories the most advanced in the world."

"Our factories are so important that we believe they will ultimately deserve an order of magnitude more attention in engineering than what they produce. At very high production volumes, the factory becomes more of a product than the product itself," Tesla said at the time.

Tesla started out as a client of Grohmann Engineering, a small unlisted company based in Pruem, near the Luxembourg border, that helped companies design highly automated factories, a source familiar with the company told Reuters.

As pressure grew to increase production volumes at Tesla, Musk decided to buy Grohmann Engineering and make Pruem a base for Tesla Advanced Automation.

As well as BMW and Daimler, Grohmann counted the auto parts maker Bosch [ROBG.UL], chip maker Intel , and pharmaceutical firms Abbott Laboratories and Roche among its clients.

Negotiations have started with some of the clients about how to compensate them for lack of resources devoted to their projects, one of the sources said.

The German labour union IG Metall has demanded that Tesla's management formalise multi-year job guarantees and increase salaries as a way to provide assurance amid management turmoil. [nL8N1HY8JW]

(Reporting by Edward Taylor; Editing by Kevin Liffey) ((Edward.Taylor@thomsonreuters.com; +49 69 7565 1187;))

UPDATE 2-Tesla hikes pay to quell unrest at key German supplier - 路透新闻

{{20170426T223606.209+0000}}UPDATE 2-Tesla hikes pay to quell unrest at key German supplier* Tesla says Klaus Grohmann has departed Tesla Grohmann Automation

* German union IG Metall demands additional job, pay guarantees

* Grohmann a key supplier to help Tesla achieve volume growth

(New throughout, adds comments from Tesla Grohmann labour representatives and union official)

By Edward Taylor

PRUEM, Germany, April 26 (Reuters) - Luxury electric carmaker Tesla offered pay rises and job guarantees to defuse labour tensions at a key German supplier, whose founder and chief executive left the company late last month, German labour officials said on Wednesday.

Klaus Grohmann, former head of Grohmann Engineering, a maker of automated manufacturing systems, has left the company, Tesla and German trade union IG Metall said on Wednesday.

Grohmann Engineering has helped Tesla rivals Daimler and BMW build production facilities for electric car batteries. Tesla agreed to buy the company in November and it is key to the Silicon Valley carmaker's bid to succeed in the mass market by massively ramping up output. [nL4N1D93YX]

Since the takeover, Tesla has given job guarantees and pay rises to the firm's 700 employees in the small town of Pruem close to the Belgian border, under threat of strike action organised by IG Metall, the powerful labour union which dominates Volkswagen .

The union said job guarantees and the offer of employee stock options have significantly reduced the prospect of a strike. Still, IG Metall is demanding a collective wage bargaining contract and improved pay. The union has complained that pay at Grohmann is 25 to 30 percent below an industry-wide collective agreement for the metalworker electric industry.

The head of Grohmann's works council, Uwe Herzig, said Tesla had offered another 1,000 euro ($1,089) one-off payment after Easter, on top of job guarantees, pay rises and stock options.

In March Tesla offered employees a pay raise of 150 euros a month. This was followed up just before Easter with an offer of 10,000 euros in stock options for four years, and a pledge to guarantee jobs for five years, Herzig said.

Herzig said Klaus Grohmann, under whose leadership Tesla had planned to run the business, retired at the end of last month.

"In November we were told that everything would remain the same, and then on March 31 we were surprised to hear that he will retire," Herzig told a news conference, adding Klaus Grohmann had not been seen at the company since then.

Herzig said the founder's departure had been sudden and he had not had a chance to speak with Tesla Grohmann's new management, despite efforts to reach out.

Tesla confirmed Klaus Grohmann's departure on Wednesday.

"Part of Mr. Grohmann's decision to work with Tesla was to prepare for his retirement and leave the company in capable hands for the future," a Tesla spokesperson said on Wednesday. "Given the change in focus to Tesla projects, we mutually decided that it was the right time for the next generation of management to lead."

A Klaus Grohmann listed in the German telephone directory as living close to Pruem was not immediately reachable by phone.

Tesla has pledged to create an additional 1,000 jobs at Grohmann, which it has renamed Tesla Grohmann Automation, as it seeks to increase output to half a million vehicles next year from around 80,000 in 2016.

The union wants to see Tesla's management adopt pay agreements and negotiating tactics more in line with what other workers in the metalworking industry are getting. Herzig said Tesla's acquisition of Grohmann made many workers leery that the company would now stop doing work for other customers, making it too dependent on Tesla's fortunes.

"We want additional guarantees given in more formal ways as an additional assurance to the workforce some parts of which need reassuring given the recent changes," Herzig told Reuters.

Christian Schmitz, head of IG Metall's Trier branch, said concessions made by Tesla to guarantee jobs were encouraging but they were not the collective wage and job guarantees customary among German unionised workforces.

Guarantees to individual workers are easier to rescind than collective wage deals that are binding for an entire workforce, Schmitz said.

($1 = 0.9185 euro)

(Additional reporting by David Shepardson in Washington; Additional reporting and writing by Georgina Prodhan; Editing by Mark Potter, Chris Reese and David Gregorio) ((georgina.prodhan@thomsonreuters.com; +49 69 7565 1279; Reuters Messaging: georgina.prodhan.thomsonreuters.com@reuters.net))

Tesla offers more sweeteners to try quell unrest at key German supplier - 路透新闻

{{20170426T160548.723+0000}}Tesla offers more sweeteners to try quell unrest at key German supplierBy Edward Taylor

PRUEM, Germany, April 26 (Reuters) - Luxury electric carmaker Tesla has offered more sweeteners to try to quell unrest at a key German supplier, whose founder and chief executive has not been seen at work for weeks, German labour officials said on Wednesday.

Grohmann Engineering, a maker of automated manufacturing systems which Tesla agreed to buy in November, is key to the Silicon Valley carmaker's bid to succeed in the mass market by massively ramping up its output. [nL4N1D93YX]

Since then, Tesla has given job guarantees and pay rises to the firm's 700 employees in the small town of Pruem close to the Belgian border, under threat of strike action organised by powerful trade union IG Metall.

The head of Grohmann's works council, Uwe Herzig, said Tesla had offered another 1,000 euro ($1,089) one-off payment after Easter, on top of job guarantees, pay rises and stock options.

He added that Klaus Grohmann, under whose leadership Tesla had been planning to run the business, suddenly retired at the end of last month.

"In November we were told that everything would remain the same, and then on March 31 we were surprised to hear that he will retire," Herzig told a news conference, adding Klaus Grohmann had not been seen at the company since then.

A Klaus Grohmann listed in the German telephone directory as living close to Pruem was not immediately reachable by phone.

Tesla in Germany did not immediately respond to a request for comment.

Tesla has pledged to create an additional 1,000 jobs at Grohmann, which it has renamed Tesla Grohmann Automation, as it seeks to increase output to half a million vehicles next year from around 80,000 in 2016.

Grohmann has helped Tesla rivals Daimler and BMW build production facilities for electric car batteries. Herzig said Grohmann had given Tesla priority over existing customers.

The takeover and expansion plans by Tesla have prompted IG Metall to demand that Tesla Grohmann Automation adopts collective wage agreements and job guarantees above and beyond an existing pledge to guarantee Grohmann jobs for five years.

Christian Schmitz, head of IG Metall's Trier branch, said concessions made by Tesla to guarantee jobs were encouraging but they were not the collective guarantees customary among German unionised workforces.

Furthermore, key parts of the workforce at Grohmann were being paid around 25 to 30 percent below an industry-wide collective agreement for the metalworker electric industry sector, IG Metall said..

($1 = 0.9185 euros)

IG Metall setzt in Tarifstreit mit Tesla auf Kompromiss - 路透新闻

{{20170426T160408.739+0000}}IG Metall setzt in Tarifstreit mit Tesla auf KompromissPrüm, 26. Apr (Reuters) - Im Streit mit dem US-Elektroauto-Bauer Tesla um die Einführung eines Tarifvertrags beim Maschinenbauer Grohmann schlägt die IG Metall leisere Töne an. "Unsere Forderungen sind legitim", sagte Christian Schmitz, erster Bevollmächtigter der Gewerkschaft in Trier, am Mittwoch am Unternehmenssitz im rheinland-pfälzischen Prüm. Das Vorgehen der Gewerkschaft sei in Deutschland rechtlich geschützt. "Wir sind selbstbewusst." Zugleich räumte Schmitz ein, dass Tesla mit dem Angebot für Einkommenserhöhungen und Boni für die Beschäftigten dem Streit die Spitze genommen hat. "Es ist doch nur ein kleiner Schritt notwendig, um hier vernünftig miteinander zu reden." Anfangs hatte die Gewerkschaft Tesla mit Streik gedroht.

Die IG Metall habe ihre Forderung dem Arbeitgeber überreicht, sagte Schmitz weiter. "Leider gab es bisher keine Zusage für Gespräche über einen Tarifvertrag." Tesla bietet den Grohmann-Beschäftigten 150 Euro im Monat mehr. Zudem sollen die Mitarbeiter Aktienoptionen im Wert von 10.000 Dollar erhalten, die über die nächsten vier Jahre ausgeschüttet werden, sowie einen sofortigen Bonus von 1000 Euro in bar. "Das würde die Differenz zum Tariflohn reduzieren." Aktuell liegen die Löhne bei Grohmann 25 bis 30 Prozent unter dem Tarifgehalt.

Für Verunsicherung bei den Arbeitnehmern sorgte, dass sich der bisherige Firmenchef Klaus Grohmann aus dem von ihm agegründeten Unternehmen zurückgezogen haben soll. "Im November wurde uns noch gesagt, es bleibe alles beim Alten. Ende März waren wir überrascht zu hören, dass er in Ruhestand geht", sagte Betriebsratschef Uwe Herzig. Seitdem sei Grohmann nicht mehr in dem Unternehmen gesehen worden. Grohmann war zunächst nicht für eine Stellungnahme zu erreichen.

TESLA BAUT AUF GROHMANN

Tesla hat den Anlagenbauer aus der Eifel übernommen und will es zu einem Zentrum für automatisierte Fertigung ausbauen. Grohmann entwickelt und vertreibt Anlagen für automatisierte Fertigung, die Tesla für den Wandel zu einem Massenhersteller dringend benötigt. Noch in diesem Jahr soll Verkauf des Mittelklassewagens Model 3 starten, die Produktion soll im Juli anlaufen.

Bei den Plänen von Milliardär Elon Musk für Teslas Aufstieg zu einem Volumenhersteller spielt das Model 3 eine zentrale Rolle. Für den Wagen, der in den USA zu einem Preis von 35.000 Dollar (32.000 Euro) auf den Markt kommen soll, liegen bereits rund 400.000 Vorbestellungen vor. 2018 peilt Tesla die Produktion von 500.000 Autos an, fünf Mal soviel wie zuletzt.

(Reporter: Edward Taylor, bearbeitet von Jan C. Schwartz; redigiert von Hans Seidenstücker.
